1401309666|5.0|The concept of the \\"Long Tail\\" is summarized by Anderson as follows: \\"Our culture and economy are increasingly shifting away from a focus on a relatively small number of hits (mainstream products and markets) at the head of the demand curve, and moving toward a huge number of niches in the tail.\\"  Anderson demonstrates how technologies today are making it cost efficient for organizations to offer an almost endless variety of products, on behalf of a different niches and consumer wants.  I found this book to be a very interesting easy read; this book gives a very clear explanation of how technology is changing the business world.  I do not necessarily think this book is for business people only, I suggest anyone in this day and age read this book because it is filled with plenty of examples that can help the consumer as well as the organization.      Anderson uses different companies like Amazon, Google, and Netflix to show how selling less of more can actually be a successful strategy.  Rather than selling one product to as many consumers as you possibly can, focusing on selling a lot of different more undesirable products to a few people is proven to be more profitable.  Anderson discusses historical models which appeals to the masses then explains new types of markets and the different practices we see today that appeal to all.  In the past only the head of the demand curve was focused on but what Anderson talks about is further down the curve which the demand may decrease but never hits zero; this concept is better known as the long tail.  Anderson provides plenty of examples and statistics that support the idea that the 21st century is more focused on niches and the internet has made it possible for consumers to obtain anything no matter how weird the product is.  Anderson focuses heavily on the entertainment industry; one of the examples used to show how the music industry has changed is there is no more top hit singles rather a different hit single for each genre of music.  Anderson also discusses how the sales of book stores and record stores have strongly decreased due the convenience of different websites like Amazon and I-Tunes which offer a greater variety to consumers.  Anderson explains how the internet is becoming the main source of shopping for consumers and if you are not a long tail business you will simply not be able to compete and will not survive.  Anderson providers readers with two tips on creating a long tail business;\\"Make everything available and Help me find it.\\"    Anderson provides statistical data and examples to demonstrate how the internet and consumer demands are changing the business world and how selling less is more.  I would suggest this book to everyone because the internet is changing how we do business in every industry and is also changing everyday life.

B00005NEUF|4.0|Around a year ago I read somewhere that one or two music magazines or some such had nominated The Strokes' \\"Is this it\\" as their album of the decade. \\"NME\\" was just one such magazine (it's a British publication). Wikipedia lists more such accolades for this album. Anyway, probably some years after this album was released, and just a few years ago I finally got around to buying this album...it must have cost me around $10 (one of those 'bargains' the chains promote sometimes), and since I loved the song \\"Last nite\\", I thought it was a punt worth taking. At the time, 2 or 3 years ago (or whatever), I have to say that I found the album a big disappointment. If I had reviewed the album then, I might have scored it 2/5...like a lot of albums, one killer song does not a great album make. Basically I thought that the entire album, apart from \\"Last nite\\" was \\"meh\\", as Lisa Simpson might say. So, for my final review on Amazon, I thought it might be 'cute' to revisit this album and fully expect to post comments like \\"If this is the album of the decade, it must have been a really quiet decade for decent music\\". I'm guessing my initial poor response to the album was that I genuinely like great radio songs...\\"Last nite\\" is my idea of such a song. Nothing else came close, though I do seem to recall a video for another single off this album and finding the music sort of okay...relistening to this album this week, I can't say that that lesser song stands out. Anyway, having recently listened to a lot of prog rock music, I have to say that the rest of the album is no longer \\"meh\\" to me. Now, I can actually point to other songs on the album and say that this song has some nice lead guitar on it, or the vocal melodies are catchy. Like Nirvana before them, The Strokes have some childishly simple guitar melodies and vocal melodies which are simply catchy. And that ain't bad. Like Nirvana's \\"Nevermind\\", which I also found extremely \\"meh\\" when I listened to it, revisiting this albumhas improved my perception of it...but nowhere near to the same degree as \\"Nevermind\\". I can't really see how this album revitalised rock music, but it is nonetheless a solid listen of pleasant and amiable enough songs. I'll put this somewhere in my list of the greatest albums of all time, but it's not in the same league as The Classics, despite gaining the tag from NME as \\"The album of the decade\\". It's on a par with The Vines' \\"Highly evolved\\".       As for the music, it's mid-tempo, with nice complementarity between the melodic vocals and the lead guitar. Australian band The Vines got bagged for wearing their influences of their sleeve, but towards the latter end of this Strokes' cd, you can make out some of their own influences. Again, what bumped this album up for me from around 2/5 to around 4/5 was just noticing how catchy and melodic the guitar and vocal parts were. Sometimes re-exploring an album can change your opinion of an album. On my first relisten of this album I gave it 77.5/100, but I liked it slightly more second time around...82.5/100...possibly 85/100 material. Album released 2001 and has a running time of 36:27. Odd fact...Wikipedia states that this album was first released in Australia...not sure why that would be so.      The classic:      Last nite - \\"/\\". Easily the best track on the album...a classic in fact, and a song which you really could view as 'revitalising rock', if you felt the urge to. Has a cool bass line and I like the complementary guitar tinkering. Also like the poppy part of the chorus.       The best songs on second listen:      Is this it - \\">[.]\\". Album opener. Intro of electro bubbling brook noises. Has a cool, slow drum/cymbal beat. Sort of pretty guitar note 'riff'. Dual guitars. Bass guitar meanders but not in a bad kind of way...the bass is actually not bad at times. Vocals sound a bit distant and the mood is one of world weariness. Guitar parts are pretty and the vocal melody is catchy at times.    The modern age - \\">[.]\\". This song seems to threaten breaking out into a killer rock rage, but never goes that way. Quicker drum beat. One guitar has note progression (seems biased to the left hand side speaker) whilst the right hand side guitar hums away. Vocal style is in the Lou Reed mould, I think. Lead guitar solo has a bit of static to it...unintentional, I'd say. Not bad as far as the guitar and vocal melody goes.    Hard to explain - \\"[.]\\". Electro pop intro with an electric sprinkler type percussion...a synthesiser, perhaps (speaking of sprinkler sounds...last year I bought the soundtrack to the slasher movie \\"Halloween\\", by its creator, John Carpenter...I never really noticed that sprinkler sound when I saw the movie...slightly annoying on cd!). The lead guitar sound and style reminded me of the Pixies' Joey Santiago. Vocals are nice and melodic, as for the lyric \\"Based in Carolina\\"...hmm...maybe this was the song whose video I saw and didn't mind the music of? There is what sounds like unintentional static on the left hand side speaker throughout the entire song. I like the different vibes that this song has on it.       The rest (in album order):      Soma - Melodic vocal and sort of oriental style lead guitar (perhaps). Has dual lead guitar. Not bad...catchy guitar at times.    Barely legal - Mid-tempo, melodic track. The vocal sounds filtered...with a coarse/shredded quality to it...intentional, in other words.  Lyrics are repetitive and seem to be sung from the perspective of a member of 'The slacker generation'. The \\"f\\" word is used in this song. Track has a little static to it (unintentional).    Someday - Interesting beat...the word \\"skiffle\\" comes to mind...probably for no good reason...I'm not even sure I know any skiffle songs! Melodic vocals and guitar. Noticeable bass guitar.    Alone, together - 1960s style drum intro (maybe I have something like \\"Please Mr. Postman\\" in mind). then you get a 1980s style guitar sound/lick...I can't really put my finger on what it reminds me of, but I probably have in mind English or Australian songs of the era...of the more 'hip' variety, perhaps, as far as that guitar vibe goes. It sounds sort of familiar, in any case. The guitar breaks sort of sound like something of the 1950s era, as filtered through 1970s rock acts.     New York City cops - Wikipedia mentions that both the album cover used in the Australian release was changed for the US release, as well as this song being dropped from the US release in the wake of the terrorist attacks on 11/09/2001.  The US release replaced this song with \\"When it started\\". ANYWAY, intro beat to \\"New York City cops\\" has an \\"Iron man\\" vibe to it. Some drum parts bring to mind Led Zeppelin's drummer John Bonham. A riffing track...sounds sort of familiar.  Other guitar parts sort of sound like a ukelele or something. One guitar part has a sort of children's melody feel to it.     Trying your luck - Bass guitar has a nice throaty growl/rumble to it. Guitar on the right hand side plays the higher notes...more jangly. Vocals are melodic.     Take it or leave it - Vocals are quite rock at times. Right hand side guitar is melodic. Noticeable bass. Outro is quite Ramonesy, or at least 1970s style glam rock...the last 1:12 minutes of the song and the last few seconds too, bring to mind these influences, as far as the riff and the beat goes.       Recommendations:      Just by the by, the other day I was in a chain store, and they played something which piqued my interest...I asked a staff member what the band was and they said it was The Strokes...it was something off of their new album, which is out now at the time of writing.  It was catchy and could be worth checking out.    Nirvana - Nevermind. 5/5. Like \\"Is this it\\",  a re-evaluation of this album by me has seen its stocks skyrocket. More of a rock album than \\"Is this it\\" though.    The Saints - Eternally yours. 5/5. A mixture of punk and post-punk kind of songs. \\"Know your product\\" is one of the all timegreat songs...it's in Kurt Cobain's top 50 records of all time. She's always willing to tell a little while lie or a lie of omission in order to spare someone's feelings or avoid her own embarrassment. When she believes her plane is going to crash, she tells the man next to her every secret she's ever kept. She goes back to her life, thinking nothing of it until she learns her plane buddy is the CEO of the company she works for. And Jack seems to delight in hinting about those secrets at every opportunity.<br /><br />Can You Keep a Secret? seemed so predictable until a huge twist made me question everything in the book so far. It was a wonderfully shocking surprise. The relationships between the characters were what made Can You Keep a Secret? so delightful to read. Emma and her boyfriend Connor. Emma and Jack. Emma and her roommates. Emma's parents and cousin. Emma's coworkers. Of course, this immediate love goes to show Emma's issues, quite obviously as her roommate points out that she can't love him having only known him a short while.<br /><br />I will definitely be checking out more books by Sophie Kinsella after having be so thoroughly sucked into this one. Can You Keep a Secret? is a light, fun book that'll lead to both laughter, tears and questioning your own deeply hidden secrets.

0316017922|4.0|Dear Mr. Gladwell,  My high school English class just finished reading your very thought-provoking book, Outliers. Our class is set up so that everything we learn, read, and write revolves around the central question of \\"To what extent do time and place define a person\\"? We have used this question in topics such as religion, naming, and diversity. Our teacher chose your book because it talked a lot about how being born in a certain place at a certain point in time lead to either great success or a lack of it. This was extremely evident in the chapters the Matthew Effect, the 10,000 Hour Rule, and the Ethnic Theory of Plane Crashes. For me, these chapters set up a very interesting way of looking at success apart from my previous view of just skill. Being a high school athlete I was really drawn to the research you did on the ages of the players on two hockey teams in the Matthew Effect. After reading the chapter and seeing the valid point you made about the oldest players in the leagues being more mature and looking more skilled at a certain period of time, I am baffled that I did not realize this playing in my own intramural leagues as a child. Now, looking back, I am in total agreement with your statement because at least in my leagues your point was entirely accurate. My only question would be whether this same point would hold up in a sport such as wrestling where the age factor is taken out and replaced with weight. This chapter had a perfect relation with my essential question because it seemed that time, in this case the birth date, when around the age cut off date of the league, led to greater success in the case of the mature players.   The 10,000 Hours Rule also fit in very well with the essential question. I found it fascinating how there is, usually, such a correlation between the completion of 10,000 hours and the success of the person. This was especially the case in your two examples of the Beatles and Bill Gates, where being in the right place at theright time allowed them to have the resources to reach 10,000 hours and then become very successful. I find it interesting in Bill Gates' story about how random and miniscule events that most likely seemed like nothing at the time to him, ended up playing such a part in his future success. For instance, the fact that he lived close enough to the computer coding station at a time where they let people use the very high-end technology, helped him reach his 10,000 hours and then in turn become successful.   The final chapter that fit in very well with the essential question was the Ethnic Theory of Plane Crashes. In this case it did not so much deal with the time aspect of the question, but the place. I found it very intriguing in the way you tied in plane crashes to the ability of a pilot to speak his or her mind as well as the culture of the pilot. I did not know that there were actual rankings of a country's ability to speak up. I see this every day in a high school environment, where while lives are not on the line, a person's ability or inability to speak up when working with others can lead to problems both for the person and the entire group. I know I find it quite frustrating when a person refuses to speak their mind. This connection between culture and amount of plane crashes has lead to one question from me. It is, knowing that some country's have the ability to speak up more often than others, would it be right to only hire pilots from those countries, realizing that it could reduce plane crashes?   To end up this letter I would just like to say that I found book a very interesting piece of literature that could truly spark some impressive debates. I enjoyed reading the different topics and seeing them through someone else's point of view.

I can't wait to get back into the car so I can hear then next bit of the story.  Diana and Matthew, and Ysabeau, and Marthe are all appealing characters, with flaws and foibles and strengths.  I won't say they seem like real people - this is a fantasy, about witches, vampires and daemons, after all - but within their world they seem real.  Perhaps that's the key to why I like this book so much - it feels real and complete within itself, the sign of excellent world-building, which is a difficult thing to pull off.  If you would like to immerse yourself in another universe, with mysteries and political intrigue and love and history and bigotry and all the complexities that make people both frustrating and fascinating, give this book a try.  I may have to buy the Kindle version just so I can read it when I'm not by my CD player.  Since I wrote the above review, I have gotten the text as well.  I really can't wait for the next installment.
0060922583|5.0|This is a great book with lots of provocative and interesting cases and information.    If you possess an open mind, are seeking more information about the world in which you live and you understand that no one (on planet Earth at least) holds the absolute truth about reality and the universe (and you trust your instincts as much or more than the \\"experts\\") then this book is well worth your time to read.  The holographic universe is based in science and is supported by many well documented case studies by not only Bohm and Pribram but many other pioneers in physics, neurosciences, psychology, and metaphysics.  The book does contain a large amount of anecdotal evidence, but, unless you consider everyone who relates a personal experience that is outside the \\"norm\\" a liar, scam artist, or nut case, many of the cases are very compelling.    If, on the other hand, you derive your understanding of the world externally, believe only what your religions (including the religion of science) tell you are true, and are not interested in learning anything that may threaten your belief system and world view then this book is not for you.    I also recommend that you take the reviews here (including this one) with a grain of salt.  Everyone has an opinion, preconceived notions, and an agenda.  I did not read any of the reviews until I finished the book so as not to (potentially) bias my opinion before I read the material.     I find it a bit disingenuous of some of those who gave this book a rating of 1 star (or 0 if they could have) when they portend an understanding of scientific principles and then use one or two data points to rationalize their poor rating.  And for those who purchased the book and then complained that they threw away their money, I suggest they first go to the public library and borrow the book (as I did) if they feel the book may not be to their liking.    There is no end to the people willing to give you their opinion on something in an attempt to either persuade or dissuade you of the topic.  I suggest you examine the issues with an open mind and then let your soul guide you as to how much, if any, of the information resonates with you.
